Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	 We, and those from our time, place over it a fine breadcrumbs mixture plentiful in egg yolk.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the maggots cannot enter the flesh due to its hardness, for there are some men with very hard hairs, it is necessary to use an instrument called "alberit", of which here is the form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	 And thus pierce the conjunctiva only slightly, not too deeply, but make it quite fine, then apply algidum as we have said; and at the completion of the work provide for the patient an agreeable bed where he may lie on his back in a dark place; let him be free from all movements except light meals, and do not move his head or turn to either side, keeping it aligned according to its natural position until tomorrow; then remove it to that same dimly lit room, test his vision, show him some things, and reapply the ligature until after seven days; it is essential that this be done neither during the hour of cure nor immediately following incision but at a later time because the water rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	 If abscesses arise, remove the oil before the seventh day and apply ointment for healing the abscess; when it is soothed, unbind the vision and place over its face an infuser to cover any day, and remain thus in that darkened house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	 And it issues from the place little by little, and transforms into its cases; be aware that no novices should meddle in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	A certain man came to us from Yrach and told us that in our region there are seen maggots causing water blisters, although I have never seen any here on our land nor read of them in the books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And they are the likenesses of maggot forms, for those who do not recognize them see only that. They are like worms properly:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And their heads from this same subtlety are pointed, and the latter in three sharp angles.
de la char sor le neis	what is done:
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	 Never arise or become variously swollen lumps, from which some appear like scorpions with many tails; and if there are such or they have been pierced by furious colors, and they turn pale in color of bone.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	 In the case of those jugs that are swollen and not infected, it is necessary for you to make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; work on its nostrils, and pour the pungent juice into them, and treat the furrows; then bandage what you have held at the subtle point of a bone, until you know that the jug is completely ossified.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains any part that cannot be covered, try all delicate sutures; and if nothing stays in place, or swelling occurs, cut as it should be; and if malignant abscesses are present, hurry to cauterize them until they become sealed and the cartilages have ossified completely, then pour oil of larch or water with wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	 If he works and moisture reaches the palate, know that it is safe; and if moisture does not pierce as it should, know that there is a jug without bone above it, where nocturnal emissions do not occur: then you must tie a piece of linen thread slightly thickened with our hands, allowing space between each one; place the patient's head within the neck opening to its fullest extent and turn until odorous secretion emerges from the neck into the mouth; many times this is done in schools for children, and it is an easy task for those who are accustom([...] to do so.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	 Do the procedure as long as you know that they have corrupted that vessel, then draw out the blood, extract the liquid, and moisten the thread with Egyptian unguent, and put it back to its place just like before; do this for III days or more, until the ointments erode all that is lodged in the vessel; and then place a seal of wax on it for some number of days until it heals, and if it needs dried medicines, use them; this is the method to purge the head, by which one distills oils and medicines into the receptacle.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be made of silver or copper, resembling an open lamp like a vessel, and conduct as such; and if you see soot, make a closed vessel for purging the head, and place the head within to absorb substances; have one hand under the head while heating oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	what is done:
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times arises in the head of the neck a disease called "telul," which grows and becomes large until it is visible to the eye; therefore, it is necessary that you cut at the beginning, and the bone quite hard, then place on fire or burning medicine; and if one delays cutting until it becomes large, be watchful if it is hard, of fleeing color, of poor sense: do not touch with iron as it is an inflamed abscess, for when one cuts once, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is from severe pain, not of fleeing color, and you see that it can be fully covered, then drain the patient and cut without fear, and treat dry and constricting things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the neck is cut and sutured
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	 Believe that when a substance of continuous production flows into one of these cartilaginous vessels, it is little effective and often in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then indeed when this occurs to anyone, look if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then join the edges together with a stitch, and treat until it heals; and if the edges are torn apart on both sides, ensure you scrape all parts of their core until they heal, then join the edges with a stitch again, apply powder to powder from dragon's blood, and incense mixture; and place over the powders a piece of lead oxide or other lead oxide material, and leave it until it shrinks by itself, then treat with ointment until healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The way of suturing is to assemble the thread: with needles, as we have said in the abdominal wound treatment; or with thread, as I have shown you.
des apostemes des levres	Treatment for abscesses on the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	When abscesses on the lips occur that are hard like grains of pepper, small and large; then it is necessary to cut the lips apart, make an incision under each nerve, take them with tweezebrought out in each part; afterwards soak the wound after applying vitriol ointment until it heals; and then apply a healing herb poultice, and treat the area of dried things until it is healthy.
de la char des gencives	From the root of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times it arises on the gums with inflammation, which the ancients called 'albulus'; thus, you must support it with forceps, and cut to its root, allowing bleeding or blood flow; then apply vitriol paste or other drying powders thereon; if after incision, it often recurs, and is cauterized again, but does not return following the cautery; these are measures for treatment.
des sordens	of sorenesses
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	s;te la crovely;
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	When treating a toothache, one must wait as long as possible before pulling it, for it should not be done hastily; for it is a matter of great importance up until there is no excuse to extract.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	 Then when the patient is strained from milking, ensure that you check for a sore gum.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	 Many times the pain troubled the patient and he thought it was a toothache and treated the sore tooth; however, the pain did not leave because of this treatment until the evil strain is removed, as we have already tried on such cases before; and when you are well certain about the aching tooth, it should be scraped around thoroughly with a firm stick to protect the gums from all sides; then move it slightly first with your fingers or delicate pliers until it is properly aligned, after which tighten the pliers securely; and let the head of the shoulder rest in its rightful place between thy joints.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	 After extracting the tooth properly without breaking it, and if there is no swelling, take one of these ointments and apply a light amount inside from all sides, then move it as you did initially.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	 If the tooth is pierced and torn, it must be filled with cloth where the roots are; and if it is gently pulled out using forceps, do not break while extracting; and work very carefully around the gums to loosen the teeth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	 Ensure you do not break it, and leave a part behind; it will return to the patient causing greater pain from the root's residual evilness.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	 Be careful not to do as the ignorant barbers do, who by their haste and boldness break the cartilage every time without following what we have described; but cause great disease in the roots that remain or from breaking the cartilage, as often happens; and when the tooth is pulled out, wash its socket with wine or oil and salt; and if bleeding occurs therein, which often happens, fill it with vitriol paste; and if this does not help, then cauterize.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the tendons, to which you will attach the first bone, are at sharp points and large knobs, without doubling when pulling the teeth. And these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	They should be of large bones such that they do not break during extraction, and made of iron well-forged, with teeth to hold them firmly in place.
de la racine des dens	From the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	 When the root remains at the tearing, it is proper to place a piece of cotton soaked in butter on for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	 As long as the tooth is softened, then apply the tweezers called 'algofri', wherein the head appears like a surgeon's probe; and within are made similarly to a file and it takes shape.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not come out with all these pincers, it is necessary to reveal the entire cartilage around the root and apply the instrument called 'althali', that is, forceps; which gives its shape.
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	man’s.
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you use this instrument which has two heads, here is its form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools used for treating fractures of the bones, and this instrument which resembles large pliers, here is its form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And be these instruments so they cannot break; and know that there are many tools for treating bone fractures; and other instruments too which are not counted among them; and the wise masters ingeniously use their instrument themselves, according to what their works and diseases show him, because there are some types of diseases where the ancients did not teach any tool due to the diversity of cases. And does not break on his limb or other bones which he searches for instruments that you have said, and helps in gestures, here is its form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And they should be large and well held to hold the bone so that it does not escape, but can keep and remove; then restore its original position with suitable medicines for this purpose, and if there is decay in the bone, and it is small, use all of this instrument.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to natural form and its shape is unattractive, especially in young women, it is necessary that you know if the nerve remains after the tooth, and it's not on the correct side, and cannot be soaked or filed down; then scrape it. And if it is sharp with the toaster, use this instrument whose form is shown here, resembling a small beak, made of iron finely sharpened at one end:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And hold the file lightly and carefully for a long time due to the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move other teeth; if it appears that one can be filed down, use this part of the file as shown by its shape.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	It is also like the sharpening of a gimlet; and as with a gimlet's teeth that one sharpens little by little day after day until it cuts; then in the end there will be no resistance at all, and if its point is too sharp and it nips the tongue, it must be smoothed down so it becomes even, so that it neither bites the tongue nor corrupts speech.
quant li dent lochent	When teeth are loose
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	 When the tooth needs extraction either by tapping or dropping, and the patient cannot press upon what it chews without salivating, having treated them with medicines that constrict, but there is no effect; if they need restraint, then use a thread of gold for it, as silver threads become greenish and rusty, while gold does not change at all. The length of the thread should be neither too thick nor too thin according to the space between the teeth; and when you straighten the teeth, take the wire and place double twists around the II healthy teeth, then insert the heads between the teeth if there are I or more, until you fit snugly on the healthy tooth of the other side. Then resume covering up to where you started removing, and gently but skillfully pull back your hand until it moves no longer; keep the wire attached to the root so that it cannot slip out again.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	 Then use pliers to grip the bone ends, and join them together, ensuring they do not touch the tongue; then let it stay as tightly as possible, and if it dislocates again, rejoin with another filament; if stable, it will serve thus for its entire lifetime, and this is the shape of the teeth and the appearance shortly after healing:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, it is reset in its place again and again as we have said; only those who are wise and patient should do this, never forming the shape of a wax seal impression of bone, placing it back where the deficiency lies, holding it firmly as we have said, remaining long-term.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	And for the tie on the tongue's ligament.
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	 Never is this ligature made from under the tongue or naturally, such as that; nor by accident of a quickly sewn wound; and the procedures are those in which you work on the mouth of the sick person, keeping his head steady, and lifting the tongue; then cut the nerve ligament wide enough so the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if there is hardness or swelling, it's a result of the wound, so twist off the ligament piece by piece; and ensure that the incision isn't too deep, near to the artery below; and after you have done this, lift the tongue slightly with warm rose water or cold water, then place a linen tent underneath the tongue; and each night, dye the patient so that they cannot close their eyes.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	 When blood flows from the wound, if vinegar is applied to it, then use the slow-burning cauterizing iron which is good for this; and treat with another remedy until healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you see it is of black or hard color and the patient does not feel it, do not touch as it is cancer; if it is leaning towards a bladder, and there is moisture present, pour onion juice upon it, which causes an odor, and free it from all sides; and if you manage to overcome it with your treatment, apply mercury powder until it becomes inactive, then return to the treatment as long as you need to address everything; then raise the lump easily and completely, and treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	For throat abscesses
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	 Never comes a swelling in the throat called "godath", and it is properly known as two almonds; when you treat them as we have said in the division, if they are not healed, be careful: if they are abscesses hard of slight substance and flesh-colored, do not touch with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	 And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch with iron, also for the bleeding; but leave it until it heals, then you shall cut it off, or it will break by itself; and if it is pale in color and the roots are fine, prepare the instrument to cover, but first make sure that the abscess is resting and at ease.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	 Then make the patient sit in front of the sun, and their head be upright, and perform work on the mouth with your hands, and press the throat with a serpent between his fingers; and it should be shaped like silver or fine iron as a knife.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can you press the tongue with this instrument and see the abscess? Take a needle and insert it into the head, then pull upward more than you can; and apply any dressings needed. Then cap the instrument on top of which is a form that seems like force; the handle is bent, one end to another, very sharp, made of iron or silver wire:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument available, use the clamps which also form a shape.
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And take scissors on one side and the other; when you have clamped one of the heads, clamp the other in the same manner, and after making an incision gargle the patient's mouth with warm water, saltwater, and honey solution if any blood flows, then rinse again with either boiled quince rinds or fennel fronds, until it is clean; and cure until healed. If no other abscesses form in the throat besides these two heads, clamp them just as you did the first ones.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	 And I healed a woman with an abscess inside her throat, which was of minor concern; and I had thoroughly closed the entire throat so that she could not breathe through the conduit being blocked, and couldn't eat or drink, and would have died if it persisted for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	 And the abscess was so swoln that I had to make an incision with a needle through its two narrow openings.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	 So I immediately did it and inserted one needle in the throat, then the vein bled greatly, then I reinserted into another nostril but could not go far, and blocked the mouth and pressed on the tongue; afterwards I inserted the needle into these abscesses, and entered part of one, only a small amount of blood came out. Thus the pathways in the woman's throat were cleared, and she began to drink water and then wine, without stopping treatment of that abscess for long periods; the abscess would grow again, and fill up the space I had emptied, until it became very large. Then I tricked it and cauterized inside her throat: thus it stayed without growing; and I left those parts, and only God knew about her afterwards.
de l’uve	The term "de l'uve" is an Old French word for the eye or a grape (depending on context). In medical terms, if we are discussing treatment related to eyes, "the eye of someone suffering from inflammaturms" would be a reasonable translation. However, without additional context, it's difficult to provide a precise English equivalent.
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	 When they resume at the eye, and it is escaped and extended, then it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is out of large and round, then it is called "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	 When it is healed as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, and you see that the abscess head subsides and becomes subtle, then you should drain it; and if it is round but not long, and it is bloody or of flesh color or black, then you must incise around it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	 For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	 Therefore, when you see it as I have described in regard to its shape and length, seat the patient facing the sun and press their tongue with the instrument we mentioned earlier; then insert a needle into the eye, pass it through, and drain at 2/3 of the depth that I said in the incision of the 2 almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	 And if the patient fears being covered, then you must apply an instrument for reassurance during the procedure.

Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it has a head or wound where you place the medicine, like the handle of a spoon, and put the instrument over all of the medicine; let the patient lie on their side so that saliva and muscle secretions flow from the mouth into the medicine without going to the throat and stomach; then hold your hand over all of the medicine and press it onto the wound for a quarter hour, until you see dizziness from the medicine subside; and if you notice, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, moisten the cotton with the medicine, and place the instrument into the cotton in the area above, until the cotton adheres to the wound; and do this frequently until the cautery is perfected, then let it dry and fall off after 2 or 3 days. The inflammation is raised to the head so that it can more easily enter the throat, and raise the head upward; and be careful not to touch the epiglottis, as it may swell or push in the bone within. de la sansue de la gorge	Please exclaim: The throat without any obstruction and no longer remains in the mouth of a spitting. If there are still remain in the mouth; or if they do not remove all the throat does not come out, so it is taken out as follows: And let be removed from the mouth.

puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet. li chapistres des apostemes	The treaters of abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	 There are many types of abscesses, as remembered from this book in one way or another, and they vary between perforation and cutting; there are two ways to do it, one being the same method but due to moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	 And the second manner is for buboes located within the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	 because abscesses on the head are different from those at the base, and abscesses in the groin area are different from those that occur in joints, each requiring its own judgment in treatment.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	 And if to treat abscesses one should not cut until the swelling is fully healed according to its progression; and for such that must be cut when ripe, and do not heal as per their progression, like abscesses near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	 When an abscess comes near the joints and is left to rot, sometimes causing impairment of the ligament and nerve in the joint, which causes contractures in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	 If the abscess is near the main limb and you delay perforation until it dies, it will harm the main limb; if it's near the root, pierce it so that it dries out completely; and only then should you pierce an absess once digestion is complete, especially near the root, to ensure it does not spread outward and becomes a fistula, which cannot heal over time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the time of perforating an abscess when it has ripened according to its completion; and this is when the pain is eased, and the departure of fever, and the lessening of pain and redness, and slight debilitation and sharpening at the head of the abscess, and other signs. It must be that you let the perforation sit or as high up from the abscess as it moved; and it should be a long perforation in accordance with the body, and if the abscess is on hands or feet, joints, nerves, arteries, or any other similar areas without swelling.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	 In those that bulge, according to that limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	 And when an abscess is in its natural place, it should be left to drain until the process of complete digestion is finished, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	 For if you pierce it from above, the poison of its contents may spread throughout the body and be filled with much filth; and sometimes the lips harden and the deeper parts become so.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	 And for any abscess that is pierced according to the size of the body, as its limbs require it.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	 And it is necessary to pierce small abscesses with small punctures and large abscesse with large ones, as well as multiple openings depending on the size of the abscess; if such an abscess requires closing its opening or sealing it when it becomes hard like cloth and dead, then do so as you would for a blister: and if there are those that are torn in three angles, or like the bellows of fir, similar to arm-abscesses; and if there are such where one makes a round incision, along with other punctures and closures.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	 For those who have a superficial boil like an abscess, you must simply pierce it easily; and if the abscess is large and has great swelling, do not drain all of its contents at once, but drain part of it; then stop draining for a day, then no longer drain anything directly; repeat this process gradually larger each time until completely emptied; especially if patients are weak in strength or pregnant women, young children, or elderly men.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	 For the boil will occasionally spurt when draining occurs, which may cause harm to the patient, and you should be cautious.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Remove this dressing carefully with great caution, and when you have noticed your abscess, open the wound, and examine if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it's a neat size, prepare tents from linen or old cotton; and if it's large abscesses, and there are many threads, then one tent must be placed in each so they meet together; and if you have cut into the sore part of the skin, and wrapped it around, then fill it with old cotton or linen rags without moisture, until three days have passed; then bandage, and treat with ointment until healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	 If bleeding occurs from the wound, treat it with cold water and ease, and wrap the area dampened many times over.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If bleeding persists, treat it properly and heal the wound, and apply the powders mentioned in this book, and if it is winter or the area of the puncture or abscess is very sensitive, wrap it with damp tents and cloths soaked in wine and hot oil; and if it's summer, and the area is fleshy, cover it with moistened cloths soaked in water and oil, or wine and cold oil until day three as we have said, then release the puncture or abscess and drain and treat it appropriaderently until healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	It is essential to know in the treatment of arrow wounds: now I have told you how one should proceed before treating arrow wounds, and this chapter explains it.
des soros	About arrows
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	 When little abscesses appear on the head, there are methods that resemble pouches like those of a tailor's needle, and there are many similarities.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	 There are those that are greasy and similar to hairs due to moisture; and there are others that are hard and piercing like thorns at the tailor, with no doubt if an arrow causes harm.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	 And the workings of circumcision are that you must try with all instruments called "intermitting," from which the shape comes afterward and what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	 Because if it contains moisture, they fall due to excess length.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	 And when the moisture is emptied, scrape without leaving any hair that contains it, because it returns if left alone; then soak a cotton in Egyptian ointment if present; if not, use water and salt, and apply to the wound until the next day; this will cauterize those remaining from the night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And so begin the cotton again as before, on the second day and at intervals, as long as you are sure it does not remain overnight; then treat the wound with an ointment appropriate until healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	 And if the abscess is large, apply it with this grease according to these long strips; and make incisions around it, scrape off all skin, and provide all treatment necessary for treating where it lies; and if the arrowhead points contrary, do as I have instructed you previously.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	 And similarly treat an abscess that is pus-filled, and with the tailor's knife and curette as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	 The swelling on the abscessed pus hole is easier to treat, as there is little blood involved.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	 And if in any of these abscesses or wounds there is no moisture present, and among the abscesses I encountered are those from an elderly woman; I found the abscess similar to a long, sharp, bleeding stone, which could not be broken; and had one struck it, they would have made a wound as if from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	 In other abscesses or wounds that come from children's heads and the roots of ears, open them as soon as possible if they are located at the most accessible place, to allow pus to escape; and treat them accordingly.
des scrophules	;t:
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	 Many times abscesses occur in the neck, and from under the ears, and in the armpits, and never elsewhere on the body, and they are numerous, and interconnected with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	 And these tumors are properly hardened at their base, just as we have said for boils and abscesses in the head; and there are many kinds of such tumors.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	 There are some that contain pus, and others that have malignant properties which do not wish to submit to health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	 In that case where you see good condition upon touching it, and is similar to the color of the body, not hard on either side and not spongy like the veins in the neck or arteries or ducts, and not deep; then one should cut above, scrape off each part, stretch out the two edges near the glands as you need (as we have said for abscesses of the head); and pull slowly but surely that you do not damage the nerve or vein, nor is there any spatulous or cutting tool that slips from your hand, nor sees too far ahead, so that you don't cut anything unnecessary.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	 And if you cut the vein or artery and it does not let you work, then put vitriol paste on the wound, or any powders that remain blood, and tighten the wound; and leave it until the abscess is soothed, and becomes softened the wound, and begins to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	 And when the blood is stopped, return to your work until it is completed; then use your knife if there are any small scrofulous swellings left, cut and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	 And if there is a large vein at the root of the scrofulous swelling, it does not suit to cut that scrofula at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread, and let it hang freely without harm; then fill the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, and cure.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	 And if you cut out the entire scrofula, it is necessary to join the two edges of the wound and stitch them now, so that there is no excess due to the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	 And if it is necessary to open at its root and drain the pus, and stitch as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Those scrofulas that have excess, open where the pus has accumulated; and puncture it as previously mentioned, depending on, then apply dressings with ointments and similar things if there is decomposition of what remains from decay; and when the wound is thoroughly cleansed, administer a poultice for healing until it becomes healthy.
de squinance	Of quinsace
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancient ones spoke and talked about the incision of the throat; but I never saw it done in our land, and that is their written word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those who have quinsace, it is necessary that the incision of the throat, called "epiglote," be made; and this cannot be helped with it, because all the veins and the main part of the illness are high in those who have abscesses hot in the mouth, or in the throat or in two amygdales.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is in the channel of the throat, it must be covered with an epiglottis to avoid impending loss from strangling.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	 It is then necessary that when we wish to split the epiglottis, we do so either above three circles or four from one small cut across, between two circles or by the quantity of the cut on the sides; and those teeth are suitable for cutting the epiglottis without any resistance, and the scissors remain long enough.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	 And if the master is apprehensive, he should extend the cowhide of the throat to the entire edge, then split open the flesh as far as it reaches to the bone; and draw out any blood vessels, if you see anything, and then seal the slit, as we have said; and this is demonstrated by the bleeding from the incision at the edge of the bone that bursts through where it is broken, and due to loss of voice; and leave the open wound covered for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed for doubting strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound so that the edge is completely smooth and free from jaggedness; then apply medicines which promote warmth until it becomes healthy.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	And if one does this before the throat is completely blocked, and the patient appears near death, with difficulty breathing.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	 Then you shall cover the epiglottis so that the patient cannot breathe through it, and they will breathe through the wound, thus preventing death; and for this reason are instructed to leave the open wound until the illness is gone, which takes 3 or 4 days. Then you shall sew up the wound and treat it, until it has healed; and I will tell you what I have seen.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	 I witnessed a maiden who took a knife and stuck it in her throat, injuring part of the larynx; and I hurried to be called for help, and found her as if she were dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I examined the wound and found blood coming from it; and indeed that she had not cut veins or arteries but only her throat, and life was flowing out through the injury.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	 I hastened to stitch the wound and treat it until it was healed; and nothing happened to the maiden except that she became hoarse in voice, but later returned to her normal state; for this reason I say there is no fear when treating the epiglottis.
de la grosse gorge	Of the great throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	 These abscesses are called "throat hernias," and they are large abscesses in the color of jasper, and occur mostly in women; and there are two ways: natural and accidental; or naturally, it has no cause.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 And the accidental cases are in two ways: one is like grease on us, and the other way resembles an abscess that comes from us through arteries; there is fear, and you should not operate unless it's a small case, and try and check everything thoroughly: if you find it as you do with grease, and does not lead to any vein, then cover it like we cap hair, and treat it all around its head, if there are points; examine well and treat it as needed until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	Here comes the next sentence to translate:
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	 There are many methods among us, of which I will tell all the resemblances; and now it must be said what the differences are between ours and theirs.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that an abscess is swelling and fever, as long as the boiling continues, and inflammableness is completed; then the fever and swelling subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	 With ours, there is neither warmth nor fever nor pain, and it contains pus, which is its own sac and follows the color of the body, beginning like glass and growing; and they are two appearances, grains or moisture, with colors as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	When you come to treat the patient, first examine and inquire about all the instrument called "intermitting", according to its form or chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	 And the method of inquiring into boils among ours is to grasp or find more moisture there where you detect in the boil and turn your two fingers little by little until you know that it has perceived the head, then remove the intruder, being careful so as not to slip.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	 If moisture runs in a vein, so it has color, then do as I have said for other abscesses; and if after the incision there is no moisture, believe that it is fatty, then dress it accordingly with cross-shaped applications, and take tweezers to lightly scrape off each part while guarding the cloth where it lies so you can treat it healthily without leaving anything behind. And if you cannot make it healthy as a whole, then cut it into pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	 If there is anything left behind, it returns many times; and if some remains a little while without causing pain, then apply the wound with certain corrosive powders, tighten the wound, and put on warm soothing substances for other treatments until healed; and if they are large, cut into two pieces of the wound and cure it as one would cure a charred wood.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	If the joints are swollen and in opposition or something else, hasten to apply a poultice of vitriol broth, and leave it on for 2 or 3 days until the wound is healed, then let the sanguineous exudation rest; afterwards return to its place as it previously was.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	 Here are the forms of entangled threads, and they come in three ways: large, medium, and small; and there are three sizes which are called "albaret", one that is called "breb", and there are three kinds: large, medium, and small, to search for abscesses of fistulae; and they are like the needles used in witchcraft, made of citrus wood or iron or silver, and those moved by wind resemble those yellow ones, and more effective for searching black leeches of febris; and there are three kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the width of the opening.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	 The forms of tumors are mostly similar to what you see here: large, medium, and small; if there are tumors that have two types of abscesses in three ways alike; and if there are tumors with three kinds of abscesse, and they come in three ways as well; and if there are tumors with two kinds of abscesses only, and they also come in three ways; and all these must be dealt with accordingly.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	 The heads of these which are cut are sharp, and among them some that do not solely cut but also scrape the skin so as to leave the vein and nerve intact; and among those inserted back into place are lashes in bunches such that the patient does not feel them at the onset of abscesses. There are three kinds: large, small, and medium, which you observe; they are only used where well-nourished, like legs, arms, nipples, ankles, and similar places; and never is a smaller instrument made like scraping lashes as per this method to stop bleeding.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is placed at no time back into its original position where the veins are tied off, and in the arteries, and never returned according to this grand form:

Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of treatment is that the patient lies on their back, with the head of the rod and the cup as straight as a pen's length so that the urine may flow easily, as it should; and guard against blood seepage which often occurs, and if it happens, use the ligature to stop bleeding and treat the wound until healed.
des pustules de la verge	And of pus-filled sores on the rod.

The cautery serves two purposes together: that is, for the flow of blood and corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, it is necessary to stuff or direct the penis with a reed pipe, and let the patient urinate through it; and when hairs are sparse at the top of the penis as in those who have not been circumcised, which occurs for wounds or abscesses, then indeed you must scrape with an instrument called chevere until the ligaments are released and freed from all sides. And if this is a grievous matter to discuss herein, it is necessary that you scrape with spatumile (a type of cauterizing iron) slightly at the head of the penis and hairs; then carefully separate between them, and place a fine linen cloth soaked in cold water upon it, ensuring it does not become completely bald.
de la circoncision	Of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not a continuous separation like other wounds; however, if we perform this work of our own will and properly for children, it is necessary that we do the best work and the easiest to health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not practice circumcision on their children, as they do not use it in their laws, and we have only what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	This is the translation of the text line by line:

Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundificación que es dou dal n'est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundificación de l'ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, y corront l'uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu'il n’ont mestier de mundificación y je l’ai veut.

De la mundificación que es feita con fuerzas al todo el lien del fio he trovado la bondad del experimento, porque las fuerzas cortan igualmente arriba y abajo.

Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of strength for purification is as follows: both heads should be held and sharp, and the head should be as large as the hand equally.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error in purification occurs when the core within escapes during incision; therefore, it is necessary for you to extend it with your fingernail, similarly causing an abrasion on the skin, and then cut evenly, and if you cannot hold it with your fingernail, use pincers, and then cut.

And if they persist for three days, and what is under the rod is swollen, leave it until the abrasion has calmed down, and lightly scrape off; then cut as you can move, but beware of the part of the rod, this will not harm him at all.
