de la voinne civile	 Of a civilian vein.
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	 This vein is found in legs, warm areas where there are no herbs or trees, and on dry land with no moisture; sometimes it appears elsewhere than in the legs, as a result of swelling that comes from under the skin like what occurs internally with serpents and worms lodged between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	 And if the signs of this vein's beginning are such that it comes in the leg as a very great inflammebtion, then its heat changes to cold, and begins the vein to flow outwards, like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	 When the head is open, you must wrap around a piece of linen 1 and a half to 2 feet in length on it, along with nails, leaving the linen attached to the leg, and every time there's no longering, then wrap around the linen, and the skin; and if it is too long, cut off part of it, and wrap the remainder, not covering it at its root until fully out, because if you cover it, it will enter into the bone, bringing about an abscess and pus or infection therein, and a bad disease; therefore, this vein must be treated little by little to completion, leaving nothing or remnants; and there is never any bleeding when this vein is treated with 5 or 10 hands' length, or one man came to me whose it had come out at a distance of 10 hands long, and when you cover it, he pours in five arrows or spears, and pierces all the way through, so that everything flows out; and remove the material inside, cleaning up with medicines for pus every day, then treat as one would an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	 And at no time through this vein hands bleed, especially when it opens in the joint of the foot or ankle, and there is much torsion, and which flows heavily; then treat as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	 From worms that grow between skin and flesh.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	 This disease is called in our land "ox sickness" because it often occurs in the bile and consists of small worms that grow between skin and flesh, moving up and down throughout the body causing pain as they traverse the skin, sometimes forcefully; and are associated with decay from various bodily fluids, such as those seen in serpents, earthworms, and roundworms or intestines. Doubt arises regarding its nature, for when it travels through the body, it often ascends to the head, reaching the eye, sometimes reentering randomly, and destroying it; this occurs many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	 When you see it to be drained and wound, one cannot force it unless it moves: therefore, it is necessary that you hold the joint above and below with a strong ligament tightly, then wrap around and draw out the foreign body, and if it seems to have penetrated deeply into the flesh, cauterize with fire until it dies; and the greatest harm it causes is that it may run in oil as we have said; and if you see it coming or near the eye, firmly pull down the eyebrow, then wrap around, and draw out the foreign body; and one must use purifying medicines for dispersing corporeal humors, and wash with putrefying meats.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	 from the pain arising from woundiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	 This disease is called 'vakir' in our land and causes pain in certain limbs, which then moves from one member to another; and I have seen what I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	 I was called to see an ill woman and found her with swollen arms, and a small inflammation in the vein of her arm; shortly afterward, I saw it rise like a worm at the shoulder, faster than anything else, similar to live silver when cut from one place to another; the pain moved away from that location, embedding into the shoulder, then spread throughout the body until reaching the other arm. Then she told me how it would return around her body as I had seen.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled greatly at how it moved from member to member, for I had never before experienced this illness in such a manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	 However, I want to maintain that anyone wishing to move pain from one place to another may do so, but I have not seen it done as in the woman; and I thought it was because women have dry bodies, with exposed veins, and thus appeared this constrained swelling; and not according to this reason are those who are illustrious, and have moist bodies and re-covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	 And when you see curing this disease, and the patient feels that pain if it opens up as we have said, quickly apply pressure above and below hastily, and then bandage until the constrained swelling subsides; and cauterize the wound; and if you do not see it with your eyes, treat as those who reduce flatulence, like foul pills and serapias seeds, and other similar things.
des saiettes	 Of arrow extractions
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrowheads are of various kinds, depending on their appearances and where they come from in the body.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	 The diversity of their arrows is such that there are some with large points, and small ones, feathered, or fletched; and those with two angles, and those with tongues, and those which have pieces; and the one that lodges in any limb does so in a particular way: either as principal members like the brain, liver, heart, lungs, intestines, bladder, and similar organs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	 When it lodges in any part of these limbs then the sign of death that I will tell you hereafter becomes evident: if it is necessary to consider extracting this arrowhead, for death approaches in various ways; and when this bad sign does not appear, and the arrowhead is not fully embedded, treat and dress the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	 And the sign of the brain when the arrow enters and pierces the bone is a swollen forehead that is reddened, stiffened, strained, and flushed with color; also inflammamoin and flushing of the tongue, spasms and confusion of understanding, vomiting of bile; and sometimes without force in the nostrils or ears; and perhaps it affects speech and voice; and there is a wound from moisture that appears as white hair, and spreading like burnt charcoal; and if this sign becomes apparent to you, then proceed with treatment, and extract the arrow if it has not come out.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	 The sign of the arrow when it enters or leaves is that it seems to be near the left wrist, and feels as if it were inserted into something hard, not hollow; and sometimes the arrow moves like hairs, and there are black veins coming out, along with chills and cold sweat, and fainting: then you feel doubt that death is imminent.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of arrow shafts is that the patient's forehead has no foam at the wound site, and their throat swells, and the ill person changes complexion, and they gasp loudly and crave cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	: the
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	When an arrow falls or from the belly, perhaps it leaves behind no trace of indigestible flesh.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	If the arrow falls into the belly and there is no exit through the intestines, then there is no hope in treatment or extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	If the arrow falls into the bladder and the urine stops flowing while coming out feverishly, and the patient feels intense pain: believe that the wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	Other limbs, depending on the face and neck and throat and shoulder and hip and spine and loins and thighs, and all resembling limbs are safe according to various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or an artery and it's not poisonous, as I will tell you what happened to me, so that you may do likewise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	 It happened to certain men that an arrow struck the first joint near the nose root; I tried it, and pierced from another side through the ear fat, and was almost sound without exception.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	 And pierced another joint where an arrow entered through the eye fat near the paper below it, and the arrow was protruded outwards, reaching only the tip towards its shaft, being large like a Turkish bow without ears; the joint remained sound, with no unexpected occurrences.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	 And pierced an arrow to the throat of a Christian; it was an Arabic arrow with ears: I removed its fletchings and subtly guided it until I pierced, leaving the Christian sound.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	 And a man struck by an arrow at his abdomen, believing he would die; and even after thirty days had passed, there was no change in his condition; I cut near the arrow, repositioned it, removed it completely, and nothing adverse occurred.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	 And for the man on whom an arrow fell on his back and the wound was swelled above it; he remained with the arrow inside him without any change in his natural disposition or harm to any of his natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	 And for another man to whom an arrow fell on his face and the wound was swelled; he suffered great pain in this manner and many similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	 And I treated a man of the king's council, in whom an arrow was lodged between his shoulders and he slightly leaned to the right; and the arrow was fully repositioned after being with him for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	 If I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	 It had been carefully concealed, and I could not feel it; but it caused twitching and pain from his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	 I thought it was the tip of an arrowhead. I placed the poultice on top, as a digestive remedy because his eyes were not swollen; and it seemed to me that I could see the arrowhead.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	 I kept the poultice on for days and allowed the wound to heal from within, until the patient felt the arrowhead in his brain; and he told it to me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	 I applied a corrosive anti-infection poultice to the wound until it healed completely and tried it out; then placed another such poultice on the opening of the wound so that the head of the arrowhead became visible to me, and thoroughly permeated around it for four months; after which I applied a remedy causing the skin at both sides to shrink, but could not remove it. Then I ceased with subtle manipulations and devised clever ways to extract it until one day, using tongs that were skillfully fashioned in accordance with this chapter's guidance, I extracted the wound entirely.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	 And the masters judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored; it will be reset immediately, and the wound is bandaged, and the patient becomes entirely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	 And I have told you the quality of arrow extraction; focus your care on what I do not mention here, for the book cannot cover everything; but wise masters discuss little about much and much that is present and failing, work with nine tools, and use nine instruments for dealing with strange matters in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	 I say that arrows lodged in limbs are of two types: those that enter at the spot or from another direction; and if an arrow enters where it is lodged, it is a penetrating shaft entering into flesh, and never comes out again.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	 If it does not burst now, let it remain so long as the joint is swollen around, and be drained; likewise if it is fixed in the bone, and cannot come out, leave it for several days, moving slightly each day; then it will burst, and if it does not burst, puncture all around a very fine hole until the cavity is widened, and then extract.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	 If the arrowhead is fixed in the bone of the skull, reaching almost to one side of the brain's ventricles, and subjecting the patient to some of the accidents I have previously mentioned: do not extract it, but let it remain until it becomes equal after several days because if it reaches the jugular vein, it is deadly.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	 And if the arrow is not stuck into the bone alone and does not reach an abscess, and the patient remains without pain for some days, then proceed with lancing.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very swollen and cannot be removed thus, then administer ointments around it as I have told you; then treat the wound until it heals cleanly.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	 And if the arrow is reset in the body but cannot be seen, encase it entirely; and if you feel it, treat with any suitable instrument; and if you cannot due to the widening of the wound or depth of the arrow, and there are no bones, nerves, or veins, then extract as much as possible when the wound is large; and remove the arrow if you can touch it, and if it has ears where it holds, cut off any parts that are stuck out on both sides that you can grasp, and then break or fold the ears of the arrow so that you can more easily draw them out; but be careful not to break the arrow while extracting.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it once, let the vein reach its limits before pulling, for extraction is painful.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	 If the bleeding occurs contrary to our instructions, follow the treatment as described in this chapter; and be careful not to incise nerves or veins, and extract arrows with a technique that avoids danger, quickly or slowly, gently or clearly; position the patient according to how they were when the arrow fell into them, for it is the greatest aid there is, and if you cannot, do so as signs show.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	 For an arrow that comes from another direction or has pierced nothing of them, or the skin is swollen in any place visible or palpable: then cut above it, as far as the pincers can grasp, and then extract; if it jumps out forcefully now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	cust that prud:
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	 If it cannot be removed, leave it for now and resume extraction as soon as possible until fully extracted; if the arrowhead is still in there, put oil on everything; if part of the shaft has been cut off, provide immediate care using appropriate tools so that the tip of the arrow enters into the tool's groove; then apply force, and if the arrowhead protrudes, insert the instrument with its point, to ease extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	 If the arrowhead is contaminated, it's necessary to remove all flesh around where the poison resides if possible, then treat the wound as needed.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 If the arrowhead pierces or injures the belly or bladder or ribs and is close by, you must cut around it if possible, then extract it if necessary; be careful not to cut the vein and nerve while doing so, then remove it, and dress the wound as needed; care for it until healed.

des voinnes dou cors communes	Of common veins in the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	 The nerves that we know are XXXI in number, of which there are sixteen heads, as follows: Two hammer-shaped ones behind the ears, called "ear herbs"; and two arteries visible on each temple; and two veins within both eyes, known as "aspirers"; and one vein in the middle of the forehead; and one vein atop the nose bridge; and the two vagus nerves that are located in the neck collarbone area; and the two facial nerves found above each lip near the mouth, which are called "augensickle"; and two cranial nerves below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	 The veins which are commonly bled in each arm: one is the cephalic, and it is on the left side, and they call them among laymen "vein of the head"; and the other is called 'fast', composed of the cephalic and basilic, and they call them among laymen "vein of the body"; and the basilic is also on the right side, and they call it among laymen "vein of the belly", and it lies under the cubital fossa, and that is the vein from which one bleeds, clearly visible above the elbow pit.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	 And the saphenous vein is the one between the little finger and ring finger, with two branches; in the leg where the foot lies, there are three veins: the first is above the cubital pit on the left side, and the second saphene which is at the ankle of the right side; and the vein called 'saphene', located in the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg there are also three veins above those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	 The source of the earaches that are after the ears helps with ancient catarrhs and migraines; and the quality of the ointment, as I have told you, is to raise the head of the patient, and rub their skin where the ears are on a coarse cloth; then tighten the neck of the patient with a band, until the two earlobes appear behind the ears at different heights: attach them firmly to your thumb, and wherever you feel hairs sprouting from beneath your thumb, hold fast; then take the lancet, and direct it into the vein below the ear down to the bone, then lift your hand over the entire vein, and puncture it well enough so blood can flow out until you see it; then tighten and tie, until it is cleaned. I have already mentioned incisions and cautery as described in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	 The vein of the two arteries that are in both temples should be treated by an ancient method known as emigrainne sodo and obtalmie acostumee, and tears from the eyes; the quality of this treatment is such that I have described: and it requires the patient to raise their head so that the veins appear openly; they feel pain in the backs of their hands, then bite down on something for relief, then lift the root of the nose upwards towards the index finger, and insert the lancet below, then draw out the blood from above, following as you have done with other veins, and bleed according to your judgment; then leave the patient lying down, place their head on cotton after an hour, then bandage firmly, leaving it until healed; we have explained in detail about their coping mechanism and extraction, or where the book begins.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	 The drainage of the vein on the forehead is as valuable for diseases of old headaches and migraines and redness, and its quality is such that patients strain their necks by twisting until the vein appears; then take the instrument called "fossoir," which has this shape:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	 And insert the tip over the vein, and hold it with your hand or another object, allowing blood to flow out in quantity as you see; then release the patient's neck and tie the vein so that it is clean and free of any broad flame-like markings.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not necessary for the folds to be too tight; and avoid being twisted, as the bone may protrude, and there's a chance of breaking the veins when they are thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	 The drainage of veins in the eyelids helps with eye conditions, redness, and facial diseases; its quality is such that patients strain their necks by twisting without ties as before; then perform the incision through the bridge, just a bit long and wide enough for slight movement, because there are no charms.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	, and let him deteres lor poilz cest cholee esproveit est to let sait isi unt, pour tout li couvide de bif menut a tet: est douce la car il est de his qui avent le fx. Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	 The lymph of the vein from the neck is as hot as ague and sciatica, and headache that comes on the face, and especially when it is longstanding; and its quality is such that the patient grips his collar, then strains his neck to your left hand, and takes a subtle, long breath, inserting it between the two nostrils as much as possible because the vein does not open well on its own, and the blood will begin to flow; do not allow it to flow too profusely and control the bleeding according to necessity, then tie it off for one night, as it is quickly restored; this is the form of the thread.
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	 The strength of the two guyots assists in stretching the alaine, at the beginning of bleeding, and many diseases, and scabs, and corrosions, and herpes, and eruptions; and the quality of the strength is such that the patient removes his collar from both sides, as we have said; and be seated with the master over the head of the patient, and the patient sits on I seat, then cleanses the vein widely for a short distance, then treats the blood promptly, or as much as necessary; then repeats in the other vein, then removes the ligature, and strains out all the veins moderately so that the patient does not strangle; and leaves it until morning when the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	 of liver disease
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The healing of vein lips above assists in coagulation within the mouth, and decay of gums, and splits of lips, and ulcers and abscesses.

The quality of liver disease is to make the patient sit before you and hold his neck as I have said; then turn the lip, and look at the veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, which can be identified by their blackness and small black vessels around them. Thus, grasp both of them, and if you do not recognize them, and are in doubt, grasp the largest ones from each side, and similarly treat all the veins above and below, for they are made in a similar manner.

Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit. Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques. Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez. Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.
