Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The inflammation in the shoulders is caused by an illness that arises from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	 The inflammation of the elbows is equivalent to that of III veins in the arm, as it draws blood from these large veins; and instructs the surgeon not to cut too deeply, for the flesh is very tender, and contains vessels and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The suction cup located on the croup is like hemorrhoids at the foundation, and diseases below, it must be large and made of wool that needs to be well milked; and sometimes, if it were too fine, it would break; causing great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The leg suction cups drain openly because they draw blood from the entire body, and are like ancient pains of the kidneys, and bladder, and stones; they reset the months and ankles, and always weaken the body after long use, bringing paralysis in various dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to apply the suction cup is that you place it first empty and quickly draw out, then put on firmly, and move evenly, without stopping until you see the red and swolereness of the skin, and appear the dull color of blood; then remove, and pay attention to the body's condition because there are those who have a sore chin, and clear pores: it is sufficient to puncture once only, but make large and somewhat deep cuts; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	When the vein is large, it must be struck twice: the first time to finesse the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the vein is very thin, it must be struck a third time; and when we wish to draw out little blood bit by bit, we do so only once at most.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	 And if we desire much blood, let us often repeat the procedure; and if the flesh is spongy, cut deeply, and finish in such a way that the vessels are quickly pierced, and for those with thick and hard skin and who have been troubled before, apply oil to the elbows of soothing and dissolving ointments: if it is violet oil, or almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil; and if it is vegetable, cress oil, or lily, or chamomile, or similar substance.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excesses are large and cold, take oil of myrrh, or balm resin, or aniseed oil, and similar substances.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	 And if the one whose joint you are strengthening with a taut and wide cord does not need oil to be applied, but rather it should be washed after ventosation with rose water, or cold water, or blackthorn berry water, or squash gourd water, or porcelain pitcher water, or other similar substance.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much sweat should rise easily, or lime water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	 And those who have large excesses should rise from old wine, or blackthorn berry water, or anet leaf or camomile infusion, or other similar substances; and they must not be ventilated before the bath or while in the bath, but one to two hours after the bath; and they should not sleep after ventilation, as it is necessary that they sweat when ventilated and when inflamed.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	 And those who are sick with colic and have too much heat and inflammation should consume cooling things such as pomegranates, endives, lettuce for ease, similar items; and fresh jujube pits, donkey milk cheese, and wet meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	 And those with cold complexions should consume syrup of honey and fragrant wine that is neither too old nor new, a little juice, fresh jujube pits, small birds, and ducks; each day they breathe deeply, they must drink more than eat; it is appropriate to give some individuals triaicle or muscat before or after ventosation to comfort the main limbs; but their heat should be subtle, only those who are hot may consume it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	 The suction cups that are placed without causing pain are those applied to the liver, and spleen, and gout, and abdomen, buttocks, legs, and hips, because these parts do not tolerate being punctured anywhere, and it is only done to draw blood from one part of the body to another, as we place them on lymph nodes when they are swolpressions; to remove the viscosity that is in the limb, as we apply suction cups to the abdomen and buttocks to reduce the limb; and alleviate pain, when there is obstruction or stones, so it may draw out the obstruction by its attractive property by chance, or remove the stone from its place; thus it works when placed on the liver and spleen when viscosity is retained, and these suction cups are prepared empty to be filled as needed; they are never prepared all at once with fire, nor sometimes plain water, as in diseases of pleurisy, and in such a way that one fills the suction cup with hot water alone, or water heated by boiling herbs suitable for this purpose.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the suction cup administered with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	 And it should have a width of two palms and a half at the front, and have around its edge a small hole, like for pushing in a needle, and be made of glass or metal, so that it does not slip on the patient when placed on the limb; and there should be another handle of transverse reed or iron to hold a candle while using it, and they come in large and small sizes according to the diseases and condition of those who use them, for children's blisters are different from adults', and thin ones from fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	 And this is how you should apply the blister: take a candle of wax or grease and place it in the middle of the handle which is also in the middle of the blister, so that when lit, the flame does not burn the patient at the bottom of the blaster; then place it on the limb, with the handles as described earlier, and wait for the steam to come out before removing the blister. Take the grease again as mentioned before, and repeat often if needed.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	 In the blister which is used for pleurisy at all times, there are no tube or valve, and it is prepared only when full of water, and is placed on the limb with great care; and this is how it looks.
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	 Blisters are prepared only for limbs where you cannot place blisters due to their small size, such as lips and gums, or similar areas; and in clean, bald wounds like pus-filled sores, take them if they contain clear, soft waters without impur grogs. Then immerse the blisters in a gentle warm water until full, ensuring nothing is inside their openings. Next, drain the blisters of blood and apply another blister; then rub the limb until it becomes red, place the new blister on top; when they are full and firm, if you can put a blister there, do so because this is very useful later.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	 If this does not work, then raise the limb with ease, and then bathe it in abundance of water, very well, and then squeeze it; and if the veins swell too much after cutting them away from the body without stitches, moisten a linen cloth in cold fresh water, and place over, until the wounds are closed; and if there are multiple wounds, apply crushed glass or scabs, among other things, until they close; or you put on the limb half of peeled beans, and let them stay until they dry to the bone, thus sealing now; and if more is needed, take additional stitches.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	 And if the wounds do not take to closing, rub fresh blood on it and insert a needle until bleeding stops, then place over, and as soon as they feel the blood, dry them; and when you see that they heal, powder with a little aloe and sage broth, or ash, so they will close now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	These chapters are often necessary in the art of medicine, and provide restoration from fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	 Know this, dear son of a bitch, that the foolish wise man delves into this treatise, which he has never seen in any ancient books nor read letters about; and for this reason, the science is alien to our land, because I have never found any good ones; and I know nothing, unless through the wisdom of ancient books, or from having studied so much that I have mastered its knowledge, and by experiment, and from the habit of my life; and I have described to you in this treatise what is contained herein, and abbreviated at the end, and shown clearly the forms of diseases that are mentioned, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, we must say in this book the essence of words and chapters where the sage places his understanding, and dwells on truth so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	 I say that when fractures or disloc cuisines, if it is necessary to support the patient on one side and another, unless nothing completely supports him as weakness of limbs, babies, or old men; or if the season is not very hot, or too cold; and consume chilled broths, that is, cold soups, fish stew, and do not drink wine nor eat any fatty meats, and do not fill up too much with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you no longer have doubt of a hot boil or leakage of matter in the limb; then the patient must return to his first state as he used to be.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary to feed the patient with foods that promote nourishment and viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, rice, barley, lamb's pancreas, eggs, fresh fish, strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For the nourishment mentioned contributes to quicker healing of the fracture.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	 And know that broken bones from the old and decrepit cannot be well mended or joined according to their nature for limb strengthening, nor those who are too flexible, like children's bones; but pay no attention, realign with strong iron rings joining the member together until it is as strong as before; and do not leave all of your work undone, and therefore you must feed on hearty meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures occur in various ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	The fracture of the head is different from that of the foot or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all ways of breaking bones.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	There are fractures that result from an upward force and others by pressure, just as the tip of a pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with a wound, or a break along the entire small split.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	 And each type has its own means and proper instruments for restoration, as memory suggests in the right place; and it is known to have broken bones when the eyes are twisted, widely opened but not far enough, and near the pressing point of the hand; and if there is no twisting or touching at the spot, and the patient does not feel much pain, then there is no breakage; however, it can still have a curvature, crack, or minor fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	by; butte and; the following an's ; siles mault that.  tad* cumbard; they aretractor; don's the de the ou let cequesteckze con ca; What. If, et sont.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	 And know that the fracture which occurs in rolling, with two parts separated, they must now be aligned equally so as abscesses may arise; and if abscesses occur, let them remain for no day until the abscess is eased; then make it equal to movement that you can easily and healthily do, knowing that the restoration of it is easier than those with missing pieces; then strain, as it should afterward.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	 And if in the bone there are broken pieces, whether main or foot, or to your hand if it's a small limb, or to two strings, or to one string and your hand; put the member according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the broken limb are dislodged, reset them by all means in their places with movements you can do, and ensure through your work no injury or pain comes upon the patient; and properly align the two ends of the bone in their best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And the patient feels a sensation in the hand if it seems to you that he is not well: dress him properly, and do not bind or press too much, as those who cause abscesses with their work often result in heat and contraction of the limb, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	 And when the limb is at a standstill, properly restrain the patient so that it does not move, neither in wakefulness nor sleep, nor turning, or any other way; and ensure the limb is securely positioned so that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	 For when it feels no pain, it is not at a standstill, and you must place it in such a position that it feels no pain; also ensure it is set properly so that twists do not occur as it heals; the quality of the damaged limb will be according to what I have told you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	the t; That:t, so they cannot we's’re assuze at se uter s (I think they should be no longer the patient of the mid.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	 For there are small members such as arms and legs: wrap them with soft fine linen; for larger ones like thighs and legs: use a wide and sturdy bandage, because the wide bandages encompass the entire large member equally so that no part is unsecured; then insert light padding III turns or IV depending on the size of the limb, and secure one hand with the whole bandage, then move to above the fracture and tighten less, as close to the fracture but slightly away from it; and gradually loosen the bandage a little at a time until you grasp a large portion of the healthy part, then take another bandage, and return directly to the injured area; then revisit the area below the fracture, and secure moderately, neither too tight nor too loose as we have previously stated in the first mention above; then place linen or cloth pads between the bandages until they are all equal, then finish with one layer of binding above them, and then apply well-made splints on top, unless there is an abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	 If there is swelling or an abscess, apply a soothing ointment for the abscess and remove the swelling, leaving it as such for several days; then wash with moist compresses made from one-third of a broad leather thong soaked in water, or wood used to make grooves, or palm leaves, according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	 But it is necessary that the stitch placed over the break be slightly larger and wider than the others; and as long as needed for small or large injuries; then secure the sutures as you did with the first one, then above a thread promptly, just like in the first stitching atop the tear; tighter means less width; it is necessary that the thread be medium-sized, not too thick nor too thin, and made of flax linen; because if the thread is too thick as I have seen in works where men make their rope ends from twisted linen threads, it's a great mistake, for the stitch cannot be equal if it is too fine, and it must not have less than two finger spaces between each suture.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is in pain from the shoulders of their arms after being strained to healthy places, then place poultices of flax or cotton rags so they do not itch.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound has been torn open and the keys are broken, I will now explain the treatment hereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not necessary to strain all the damaged limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	 When the limbs are large, it is not necessary to put them in splints unless after 5 or 7 days, or more depending on the certainty of an abscess occurring; and here is the manner of ancient surgeons for restoring fractures, dislocations, and torsions: take flour that stands against the walls of a mill, mix with plenty of water, creating this concoction which should not be too clear nor too thick, and use it. This is the common method of splint used to restore broken limbs in various conditions, especially for women and small children, as it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of plasters for restoring fractures, dislocations, and twists: take abareis (abarotum), ladanum, aniseed, asphaltide, gum arabic, and myrrh - .x. Z.; aloes - .v. Z.; alechilengrae - .viij. Z.; make a powder of it, mix with egg white; if the patient's humour is hot, use this plaster as it has good composition and quickly restores broken bones in many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	 Another method of splint for torsion: take myrrh and wormwood in the amount of 10 scruples; cassia and aloes in the amount of 9 drams; acacia in the amount of 6 drams, frankincense in the amount of 10 drams. Grind well, mix with water or plenty of whey, and apply.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	 Another way to reset dislocated joints and their bones that have come out of place; it alleviates pain occurring, and the cutting using bone; breakage: take new linen, and milk in oil heated, and put on them at the site.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	 These plasters do not restore but are good to soothe a hot abscess and properly ease pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of treating bones that heal: take dried leaves of figs and leaves of the earthly pawl, grind them together to make a poultice.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	 Another way to reset the fracture of bone and soothe them remaining from an abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	 Take root of wormwood, chamomile, flowers of violets, wheat flour, each part; and grind it, and mix with wine, and if the member is swollen, then with water mixed from coriander leaves or just water, apply.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	 Another way to reset is more common than the first when an abscess comes due to member restoration.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	 Take root of vismalve, and seed of flax, balm, mallows, and celandine; and flowers of violets and chamomile, all together in equal parts. Then grind it up and mix with salt water or fresh water, or wine, according to the warmth of the member, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Ypocras states in his book that one should not apply anything more than a piece of wax and oil to the broken limb for healing, and it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen believes that on the broken limb for healing one should apply dry things a little warm like myrrh and aloe and incense and similar substances, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to treat pain and swelling: take mugwort and devil's claw herbs, or feathers of birds, and wormwood, in equal amounts, grind them all together, and make an ointment from the mixture.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And then loosen them a little afterward and be sure the patient feels no pain or has moved any bone from its place; if you have patience and do not rush to reset it, but carefully. If there is pain at the site, or itching, feeling of relief or swelling comes, then quickly loosen it again and remove the splint now; take a light bandage, a moist sponge in seawater, and dip it into water, and lift the limb until the itch subsides, and pain is soothed. Then let the member rest for an hour, and then apply dry cloths, wrung out with warm water or oil roseatum, and wrap around a nut (a gauze bandage), as long as you are sure of healing heat; and rest the inflammation in the limb, and alleviate pain, then resume gentle splinting again, but do not apply too much force as before.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that inflammation and redness and pain and swelling are present throughout the bone, and there is need of emollient powder and bandaging, as you did before similarly.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	 If it does not arise in the limb anything as we have said, do not reset until after III days or IIII or V or VII; and never leave more than XX days without checking its condition while healing continues, and approaching joint alignment above; then you should securely reset initially, and swell subsides with flesh growth, as I mentioned before; and if the site appears dried beyond necessary, know that scars will not form; thus moisten it with warm water every time you reset, once a day, and gently cleanse the area regularly. Through this method, scarring is prevented in the limb, restoring proper joint alignment like skilled surgeons do: anything else I see does not seem beneficial or correct.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of various ways of fractures
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	 There are many ways of breaks and various shapes, and the causes are distinguished; for there are breaks that are made from a sword's percussion strike, where the shaft hits all the bone up to the joint which is below the bone, as with an axe or cudgel; hence this type of break is called "haichure.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	When the sword pierces the bone above, this type of fracture is called "absolute"; and there are wounds from these two large or small breaks.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an impacted fracture, crack, or bone chip from a stone fall, or other similar injuries.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a persistent fracture, which extends just up to the tissue below the bone, or upon it, and this wound may be large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	 And if there is a wound that has been filled in with bone as fine as hairs, and it is a small fissure, hence this break is called "capillary"; and if the wound is caused by being struck by a stone or falling, or similar things, where part of the bone enters within, and the ends above are like when chandeliers tip over onto their candles; so between the fragments inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	 This occurs more often in those who have wet bones, like children's skulls; and it happens in all these ways of fractures where small fragments are left loose as if they were such; and I will speak about them in their proper place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all ways of fractures by the extraction near them, and the examination with tenting, and by the corruptible wound that is upon it.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The resemblance of hair is known by what happens when the bone is discovered and rubbed over it, then there are black cracks.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, beware if an unfortunate event happens to the patient, and if you see any bad signs such as vomiting bile, loss of consciousness, extension, paleness, fever with chills, eyes protruding outwardly, and other similar conditions in various states, he cannot cure without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a hopeless case, and expect recovery, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	When the pain first comes to you, and it is in winter, one must remove the bone before the fourteenth day that can be seen.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is summer, then hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the flesh above the bone is not corrupted, and the accidents we have mentioned occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	 And if the fracture of the bone reaches close to the tissue that covers the brain, then you must split the fractured part as such: and ensure that you remove the piece injured by the patient's malady, and expose the bone in all ways possible, and on top of the wound shape as much as you can; if there is bleeding when revealing the bone or pus, aid with what is appropriate, and it is that you fill the cavity with gauze soaked in olive oil; then let the wound rest until the abscesses are calmed, and be sure of the cessation of bleeding; then begin around the bard to remove, and this is done according to ways of surgery: one way is that you cut at a narrow space in front, which is its shape.
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	Then make another larger incision than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you have various thrusts of different sizes, some narrow and others wide, with points, and made of iron; and in lighter work, do not hit the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is too hard and tough, it requires that you pierce around it, administer thrusts with needles, not too deep into the skull or on its tip, leaving a margin or circle so that the point does not pass through the bone; and you must have several of these, each coming to the surface of the bone as needed, having needles for all tests (examinations); this is the form of the three methods of needles:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality of piercing around the broken bone is that you place one needle on the bone and turn it with your two hands until you know the bone has been pierced; then move the needle slightly to another spot, and do this throughout, then use scissors for the space in the b
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	 And when you have the bone pierced and broken, it is proper to treat the preparedness that has been of the bone with any other instrument similar to a chisel, but it must be more careful and subtle than the other chisels; and if there are no small bones or scales remaining, gently move them with small movements; then tend the wound with bandages and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another method of treatment is what the Galenists say, which is more salty; and it should be applied strongly, as instructed.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you expose a part of the bone where the break moves openly; and once you have uncovered that part, place it under the head of this crescent-shaped incision instrument, which has the following shape.
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	 And do not cut through it entirely, and the part is in two sides, so that the cutting tool is towards the bone; then strike with a small mallet underneath, so you chip lightly around the entire bone without harming the covering, for if it's close to the bone, chipping should be gentle, as we do not want to damage or injure.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	If the bone fracture does not penetrate through to the cloth, and the bone is cut smoothly above, leaving small pieces, then you must address the roughness again, and remove scales with a subtle razor of which you should have various quantities in order to apply most conveniently in each place according to the treatment and figure of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you have many razors, use coarser ones first, then finer ones, and continue in this manner until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each other haircut and subtle fracture, you must treat it according to its readiness; this is something that cannot be easily replaced for someone who has put their study into this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	 If the scab is uncovered, it is necessary that you take a linen bandage according to the quantity of the wound, and anoint with oil roseate, and place it upon the wound; then take another bandage folded in two or three layers, and anoint with wine and oil roseate, and place it over the first bandard. Do this as gently as possible so you do not burden the sinew, and administer above the other linen without excessively stretching it until only the wound is covered; leave in such state for one or two days until the swelling subsides, then remove it, and apply medicines as with root of lis, and wheat flour, and incense powder, and aristology, and similar things. From these things make a fine powder, and place upon the wound, and administer usual remedies without causing stinging; ensure that the wound remains clean, not allowing ointment or any swelling to accumulate, as when bow is gathered on the cervical bandage, it will tighten and restrict, leading to great harm because when you place something sharp upon the sinew, it binds.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore be cautious, if by chance something comes to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful and without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if darkness does not come due to the medicine applied, so that it may have its virtue, then you should take a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil blended with woolen cloth, and apply it on the sore; then treat as necessary according to the remedies required until healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	One says that the two parts above, or one upon the other, are not broken since they are bones; and that which lies beneath is cartilaginous, and does not break but only fold or twist, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	 And if one of the two parts is broken, then you must sew a small hole or tear on the outside and place the break inside your index finger, and through the forearm toward the thumb until it heals according to its natural form; do this gently, and ensure that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is above the shoulder blade and cannot bring the arm back to its place, you must align it with a small piece of iron rod.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	 And if the break is in two parts, then do it again; restore within one day if possible; otherwise after seven or eight days once the abscess has calmed down, then stitch up the outer part with linen thread if the break is on one side.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	When you bind another piece on the other side, if there is a breakage; and let the tendons be so thick that they fill the pores of the nerves.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	 And some surgeons say you must moisten the tendons with butter, and change it each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	 It seems to me not quite right, but it should be moistened with a mixture of egg yolk and flour powder; then leave the tendon until the bone is firm, and the cartilage hardens.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And never put goose feathers where the tendons are, and if at .i. sheep's skin strap, and holds the breakage, and blows on the sickly weaklings among them; do this that you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	When abscesses occur near the nose while working on them, apply a poultice of cheesecloth or cotton soaked in rose oil, or use a small amount of diapron.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if there is no abscesses, then apply a poultice with barley flour and incense powder, mixed with egg yolk; then place it on light gauze, not binding too tightly; and if the crack of bone fracture is small and broken into tiny pieces, extract as much debris as suitable for this case, then split open the wound, and cure foreign objects like glass or sand with suitable plasters and ointments; and if there is no internal damage to the bones, then dress the tendons, and apply linen compresses until healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	For a dislocation of the jawbone, reset it as follows: hold the head firmly between your hands and gently but steadily guide the jaw back into its correct position.
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	; do not be.s. I: an boster by theme the lion is to the sebt and asue
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary that if the fracture is in the right part, you place your index finger of the hand into the mouth of the patient; and if the fracture is on the left mandible, put your index finger from the right hand, insert the fracture gently, and adjust it with the other hand afterwards, making them equal.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jaw is displaced into two pieces, it is proper that you stabilize by extending those parts until they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if there are movements of the teeth or dislocation, strain them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then put on the fractured jaw, and place a double cloth over it; and put over this cloth a large well-made plank, or a piece of leather equal in length and width to the mandible, tying it below where you can move. Then command the patient to rest and consume light meats.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	If you see that the shape changes, reset it on the following day and then put back what is changing; place a poultice over it with fine powder from a mill or wheat flour after you have removed the clot; place a light cloth over the poultice, and if the poultice swells, ensure that the patient's position does not change, let it remain as long as necessary; many times it is healed within three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	If an abscess arises, treat as we have said many times before.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, ensure no bone fragment remains; gently remove the splinters from that area.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, expand it with fat according to your necessity.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you have moved all the bones to their places and they do not remain still, thus treat the wound if it is wide, and place over it one or two splints made of covered wood until healed.
de la forcele	To strengthen him
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The fractures break in many places before the shoulder, and the breaks occur in three ways: one is broken and separated into two, with fragments, and it is easier to restore; or there are breaks with wounds.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	This is the fracture when it's without wound, so have two ministers: one anoints the dislocated joint that feels strained; and the other extends the neck towards the part; then put the fracture in line with your arms such that its form is as required, and there be neither appearance nor imbalance.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend further, place under the patient's shoulder a round rod of cloth or linen, and make it as thick according to your necessity; and push in and release the strain, holding the rod with your hand, so that you set the faster equal as required.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the joint forward because it comes out to one side, so that the patient lies on their stomach, and places in front of the shoulder a mid-sized earthenware dish, and puts both ministers under the shoulder, until the bone of the joint is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then approach the fracture of your legs, and if you find broken pieces, it is necessary to cut into them; remove the fragments gently, and if the bone cannot join by any splinting method, use one of the tools you have prepared but place it carefully to avoid injury.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	 It appears like a spoon and is not sharp, and should be as wide as necessary according to the size of the bone and strength of the flesh; it has two heads, as you see, one wider and the other narrower, as per the direction of the wound made when setting the bones; and when confident in a hot abscess, cut the wound accordingly, if doubtful of a hot abscess, patch the wound with cloths and bandages according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	When an abscess comes there, then apply a cloth soaked in oil rose-colored and with ease, and place on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	 The straining of the bone when it feels tender and painful is that you put on the bone pounded powder of molten lead and ox fat, along with light poultices underneaturally placed over the wound; then take a very large bandage one palm wide, then place double cloths above the poultices, and the powdered lead; then take a slender plank three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around that bandage so that the head of the bandage hangs evenly. Then place the board over the fracture, turning the bandage under the knee, and above the good leg; apply pressure to each part, and when you see that the splint holds the fracture steadily, treat it gently every day, and if the ligaments are weakened, restrain them; have the patient lie on their back, and place a small pillow under the knee, to raise the dislocation upwards. This will relieve the pain from the injured joint by positioning the shoulder correctly, or binding the arm at the neck without any ill consequences until XX days; then start with the powdered lead again if needed, and continue straining and leaving it as such, until fully healed; it is usually restored in no more than twenty-eight days for most people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Of shoulder fractures
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	 Occasionally the shoulder is broken or displaced and it should not be moved except by touch; if it's set according to the pattern of the breakage, and aligned with its natural shape in all ways you can; then put on the place powder from finely ground meal with plenty of egg whites, and light cotton wads; then put a wide and subtle plate over it, slightly wider than the shoulder, and if any part remains unsupported by the pad, use linen bandages to evenly cut through the bone. Then strain firmly so that the plate does not move from its place, checking the ligament each day; whenever you feel movement, tighten again, and ensure the plate is secure if it has moved from its position, resting your patient on their back. After twenty or twenty-five days, remove the device, but be cautious because bones do not regain strength easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut. de la brisure des costes	Of rib fractures.

de la brisure dou col	Of the break of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	No fracture comes to the bones of the neck, and rarely does it bow; likewise with the spinal column of the back.

And when this occurs in any individual, and you need to know if he will be healed or not, take care if you see his hands become softened, swollen, and lifeless, unable to move or stretch them, and when pricked with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure. And the cure is to apply warm oil or sheep fat if there is an abscess, on the spine until it is eased; then place it under one of the comforting and drying stones, bind with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; do not sleep on that part where they feel pain until healed.

And if any bone is dislocated, cover it with cloth; then reposition the bone and sew the two edges of the wound together if they are large, using an aromatic ointment containing charcoal until healed; and if the shoulder blade is fractured, known as "chiés de la kowe," put your left hand pouch on it, place it equal to your right hand's power, then apply an emollient stone and thorn underneeby, if needed; then bind it tightly, and if there are any bones dislocated, treat them accordingly, realigning the bone and caring for the wound until healed.

de la brisure de l’ajutoire	Of a break of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulders are what is between the elbow and the head of the shoulder; if it is broken, then it should be restored according to one of the two ways: where you take a piece of fresh bone, in this manner.
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two heads with two ligaments, and place them upwards, then lay the patient on top of it; then pour some blood into the broken bone until it reaches ease, and let there be a bend in the wood halfway, then place under any heavy object or extend it by ministers; then set the screws so that the fracture is equal to his hands together, as long as the fracture returns as it should.

And if an abscess occurs, do not tighten until after six days, and apply a linen bandage with ease and oil rosemary until the abscess is soothed; then tighten it, and the manner of tightening should be that you place an iron over the fracture, assemble the arm above the shoulder blade, and put your hand on the shoulder or side; then wrap a cloth around it, and tighten above the shoulder blae, and along the arm so that the arm is in its proper position unless something prevents it, or if the bone has not moved.

de la brisure du bras	The translation of "Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles" would be:
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "foscile," one small and holding the elbow, the other large and located above the small joint; sometimes the large "fabicle" is broken only, or the small one, or both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	 When small blisters are burst, the healing is easy, and the treatment; when large ones burst, it's a bad curement, more painful than when they all burst together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	 If only small blisters are burst, then it should be stretched lightly and kept even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	 And if it is the large blister, then it should be stretched more firmly; extend using a splint, and raise the hand's sleeve higher than others, while smaller ones remain lower, cross them with the patient himself, placing the splint in front of him taller so he doesn't feel any labor; then extend the minor ministers towards the part below his arm or to one another, placing other ministers accordingly.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	 And then place the mirror evenly, according to its best shape.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	In case of a break into pieces, place each back in its position; if any are out of joint causing the bone to be disconnected as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And in case of a wound from the fracture, discuss it with each individual physician; if they take care.

Then remove the dressing and apply a paste of powdered medicine with plenty of heat, place the splints, ensuring that the fracture is more securely held than others; it must have VI splints or arms arranged in various ways: whether the fracture is in one bone or two; and strain more on the site of the fracture than elsewhere, as mentioned at the beginning of this chapter; and let the bandages be soft and moist, not too hard or rough; and use linen threads for binding, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	 And reward the member and the ligament after certain days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	 And if any accident comes to the limb, like itching that comes upon the limb, you shall bathe the limb in warm water until the itch is soothed; and let the limb not rest too tightly.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	 And then resume the binding, and if the ligament is softened and the bone healed, along with similar matters, you may proceed.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if there is no swelling coming to the limb because it is too tightly bound, you must first loosen it slightly; and let it remain thus for several days until the swelling subsides, then proceed with the straining.

de la brisure de la main	Of a fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	One must know that on the back of the hand there are few fractures, and it does not occur but rather frequent bending many times.

Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	by themt ja peull'* a ben the ou Rechin;s cute.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	When the fracture is in the forefinger, it is proper to place a rod on top and another underneath at the sole of the foot, so that the hand remains open and straight; then wrap the entire arm with bandages, ensuring the ligament between the bones is tightened.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.
