Be cautious during restoration and abscess placement, and treat any bleeding as previously described.
de la cuixe brisie	In the case of a broken hip bone: Take care to immobilize it properly, apply a splint or other supportive device as needed, ensure proper alignment for healing, and manage pain and swelling with appropriate treatment methods such as rest, ice, compression, elevation (RICE), medications if necessary, and follow-up medical evaluation.
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bone of the thigh is often broken, and it can be seen when it twists forward and backward; and its restoration involves placing a leech on the fracture site, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on their face, then each healer extends their hands equally over his parts; and this is when the fracture occurs within the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	 And if the fracture is near the root of the hip, let one ligament be toward the wrist, and the other ligament from under the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	 And likewise if it is near the knee, then let the ligament be by the knee, and the extension downwards; then place the mirror on the bone equally with both hands, so that it conforms to its natural figure, and then put the splint, and bandage, ensuring no infection arises.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	If there is an abscess present, leave it to heal and then return to your work and treatment; the incision is made in part.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	 It is necessary to wrap around the fracture with one or two layers of doubled cloth and leave excess material; then turn the leg until the heel reaches the root of the thigh, and thread a long string between the hip and the leg, under the knee; let the end of the string be above. Then turn the leg and thigh again, wrap them with bandage without tying it too tightly at first, then start to tie firmly three times or four times around the fracture; as you move further up from the fracture, make the binding looser. Then return to the two heads of the string that were threaded between the leg and thigh, insert three pegs above them, then back to where the head of the filament is underneath, until it reaches the foot; if the bandage does not move from its place, leave it as such, but if there are no signs of infection or swelling.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if this happens and the fracture occurs again as we have said many times before; and if there are pieces of bone that protrude, then it must be handled (if possible), and if not, then the area should be cut open, and pulled out; and treated accordingly, as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	At no time is the thigh broken so that pins are inserted as with the shoulder and arm; however, in such a restoration made, it does not at all relieve the patient's pain.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the thigh is restored in one or two days, or less or more, depending on the various constitutions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	From the groove of the knee joint.

de la brisure de la jambe	Of leg fractures

And if both bones break together, the leg turns at every part.

de la brisure des os dou piet	From the breaking of bones at the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no fracture; however, the bones of the foot do not break and the shins are not affected, nor does any weakness occur in certain conditions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a fracture of the foot bones, and you see these bnads protruding from one another, place it so that they are slightly raised off the ground, as if intending to walk; then put your own foot under theirs, where the bones have risen, and press until they return to their original position; then apply a plaster and dressings, placing two small pins through the belly of the foot at .ij. chiés plaints [places], then straighten it as quickly as possible, after which you should wrap with bandages around, and other things that are necessary.

If any of the bones are broken, then repair them as we have said for the hand's bones; then put a stake to the broken bone according to its length, and make it slightly wider, then place beneath the foot the board that I mentioned, and press together immediately; and if there are two or three or more, break each one and set a stake according to its size, wrapped in a single linen cloth, and fasten the board under the foot; so they may align with the abdomen above the foot.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And it is important not to forget other things that I have said about other fractures, as we have discussed; and treat each injury as necessary.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	Regarding the breaking of the bone in the wrist
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When the bone of a woman is broken, if she lies on her back, then tilt towards the less painful side and be supported from behind; then fill the bladder with cotton wool as thickly as possible, and place it there; then have the woman stand up slowly and gradually lift her back until the cotton ball reaches near the entrance of the vagina, and returns to its normal position. And when she needs to urinate, remove the cotton ball, and once she has finished, reset it, thus doing this for seven days or so: if properly done, the fracture will be healed. If you want further reinforcement, take a pig's bladcuase, tie cloth around its opening, fill it with water; then blow through the cloth until the bladder is empty. The vagina will regain its shape; then fill it again with cotton wool and leave it like this for several days until healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	 And when the bone of the forearm is broken, or in a woman, restore it as we have said in the thigh bone; and these fractures are not hidden from those who apply their study and effort to my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	 For a fracture indicates various conditions for the proper course of restoration: therefore, so it is.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	And when the li les cil est le sait, as it qui pren que tostide l’est de. Et vous le la dote et ne puis les boute quant il quis vient l’ent, si la ou met les jors ce qn ente la gue, dont fie espleez. de brisure avec plaie	Of fractures with wounds
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for those with fractures and wounds, especially if they are large like the bones of the hip or shoulder or similar, that they be properly aligned as we have testified with our witnesses.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healed, and there remains a stain of vitriol, unless you have something else, then begin to restore the fracture at that same hour or day, if no abscesses appear.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	c, and tot;k; thatchtiq.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone is broken appearing underneath the skin, it must be gently put back into place with your hands, through slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension does not allow you to set it even with your hands, then use this instrument made of iron, which has six or eight prongs and its width depends on the size of the wound; and so it is necessary for the physician that he grasps three or four (prongs), according to what he needs in each bone-breaking cure; and let them be round and somewhat thick, so they do not buckle under pressure on the limb you are working on, and placed with some space before it:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	 And it is called "palanquin", so the patient's head must be placed under the visible part of the bone; and be bound once, until they recover, ensuring they are even against each other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	 And if the fracture is subtle and the swelling cannot properly grip the bone, it is necessary to cut off the head of the bnage so that the swelling can have access.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot bring the bone back together as we have said, with a fitting instrument whether it is cutting or drilling, to your ability; then remove the piece that remains in the jagged and small splinters of the bone.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	 And when the bone is returned to its place, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural position.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	 If you do so that it is in its place, then make the dressing with a sticky black vinegar bandage, and properly put as if on an ulcer; and do not apply any ointment or other substances to the wound, lest it bring rot and decay. Then provide balms once you have restored the bone, leave the wound exposed, cover with a dressing entirely around, according to the quantity of the wound, and ensure it is well guarded so that the wound is not strained along with the break; and many times the foolish healers have done this and brought about death or corruption. The tension should be more gentle and flexible than other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	 And if the wound is large or bad, and you suspect that an accidental injury may occur as we have said, and you find pain at the site, then it is not necessary to place bandages; but wrap around it, at the location of the bandages, with durable cloths.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	 And when after one or two days there is swelling at the wound, if it seems that what you placed above has begun to work, and you apply a healing salve for wounds, as with Tetrapharmacist's ointment and similar substances.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary to loosen the limb twice a day, in the morning and evening, until it becomes relaxed and healthy.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is important that the limb be fitted with an appropriate splint so that the bow moves slightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if more than one day passes, and it cannot be relaxed but remains bent again, as there are small pieces of bone, then you must dress the wound with gauze and remove all those unwanted pieces that cause pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	 And if a fistula appears at the site, or other form of decay, it is necessary to treat it as described in this chapter above.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	 When the bone is broken and exposed on the limb, like the hip or shoulder bones, as well as other similar large bones, do not attempt to reset it, for many times this results in death, but leave it until it heals; sometimes it may rejoin after XX days or XXX days, then treat the wound if you know how; and if you don't, just let it be.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	From bruises coming over the swelling
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	They often come after the healing of the swelling, especially when it is near the joint, and an unpleasant thing to see is how the limb's shape changes; and sometimes cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Therefore take care if the patient is warm: if you administer medicines such as aloes, incense, myrrh, and frankincense, and any other similar substances; whether you use none of these or all together, mix them with astringent wine, vinegar, or rosewater; place it in an ointment tube, strain well without letting it separate during the day; then dislocate, and repeat with another until the swelling is gone. Or if applicable, stretch over a piece of plaster precisely made; because the property of the plaster is that it removes all inflammation from the limbs; and when the hardening has occurred like stone, and there's a need to remove it, cut off any excess on top, and treat until healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	A limb which is weak after healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is restored and remains weak and delicate afterward due to many causes: one being because it was tied too tightly, and not loosened as it should be; or because there were too many ligatures, preventing proper circulation in the limb; or due to excessive bloodletting; or from making large movements at improper times; or because there is little blood within its body, thus being weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the treatment is to have the patient eat nourishing foods and keep their body supple until blood circulation increases within them; also provide bathing care and give joy and comfort; then apply poultices on the limb, so that they draw significant healing nutrients into it, and frequently change with warm water until proper circulation returns to the limb; and let it regain its natural form.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	After healing of the limb becomes twisted
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	After the limb becomes twisted following its healing, and bones are broken openly, and the shape of the limb is unsightly: however, do not believe those who say that you must break a new limb entirely, and many foolish people have done so in our land; such treatments are blameworthy, leading to great harm, and sometimes death. However, if nodal tissue and twisting are recent, it should be treated with hot water, or soft herbs cooked as meadowsweet leaves, roots, mallow seeds, etc.; and a medicinal poultice is made, like well-prepared diaquilon, taking the muskroot of mallow, mixing it with pig fat or flaxseed oil, making an ointment; or take juicy figs and grind them with hemp seed, along with similar remedies that alleviate swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	 Never is there an issue with bone dislocation from continuously rubbing for a long time with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	 And provide some movement to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twisted and hardened tissues are like stones, they must be removed with iron, up to the bone as needed by carefully using a delicate incisor; then place cotton and focus on treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs, if it must now be returned without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	 Because if you delay, the swelling may increase and it might be difficult to reset in place; therefore, do not move it at the hour when it is swollen: many times this has caused inflammeboils and other pains; however, once that occurs, treat the patient well, then leave them alone until the swelling subsides; then bathe the limb with warm water and oil, then gently exercise each member as treatment naturally dictates its location.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	se pe en the ciles ke la dur:
des mandibules	Of the jawbones
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Sometimes the jawbones are slightly dislocated from their usual positions and become a bit soft; or they may be entirely dislocated and hang towards the left side, causing saliva from the mouth that cannot be held in and prevents closing of the mouth, wrapping its tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it can result in various positions returning by itself at times.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	 If it is complete and accomplished, you must quickly reset it without hesitation, positioning in such a way that the minister dampens the patient's head, placing two drops of ointment from one hand at the root of the mandible dislocation inside the mouth if the dislocation is between both halves; the other hand should be free to ensure evenness. Command the patient to soften his jawbones and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And places the mirror so that it is centered, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if the resetting causes pain, especially when both jawbones are together; then apply warm water and oil until they can be gently moved again; do not force them to move as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	 And when they are evenly reset and the patient's mouth is well softened, place a cloth soaked in ointment made of rose oil and wax over it, then lightly bind with soft linen strips; let the patient rest on their back with their heads between two pillows such that they do not move to either side or strain, but gently eat tender meat as long as the pain subsides and the jawbones are anesthetized. Then have them enjoy what they desire lightly, without forcing themselves to open their mouths for eating or drinking until the mandibles are well numb and healed.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	If the two jaws cannot be put back in place within an hour and are not restored to their original positions, fever and other accustomed symptoms may occur, and possibly intestinal perforation, or perhaps they vomit with pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know it is peritonitis; and many times the person to whom it happens dies within seven days.
de la forcelle	of a gland
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The strong ones cannot be dislocated from within the ribcage and below, nor can it be dislocated once in a while without effort, yet they feel it deeply.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	 And the restoration is such that the patient lies on their back and extends their arms; then press firmly with your palm to reset it, and it will return; then place over the splint and wrap it around, securing it; and the shoulder which is towards the cushion cannot dislocate again; if not, and if it does dislocate at any time, then reset the joint back into its original position as we have said; then place over the splint and secure it with a bandage, comfort the patient to rest until they are healed; thus similarly return the shoulder blade when displaced from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Of the shoulder's dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	 One must know that the shoulder dislocates in three ways: one way is to dislocate towards the ankle from above; and the second is towards the lower part of the thigh; and occasionally upwards, which happens rarely; and it does not dislocate backwards or inwardly for the shoulder, nor internally due to nerves. It often dislocates downward towards the leg, especially those who have little hair on their chest, as this happens quickly; but for those with enough body hair, it occurs slightly and re-enters easily.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes this occurs in certain individuals with swelling or bruising of the shoulder due to an abscess, and they believe it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore, you must examine it thoroughly until you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	 And it is known that dislocations occur when it descends towards the armpit, and there is a difference between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find their variety manifest; and you will find at the top of the shoulder a hollow, and below the armpit near where the head of the shoulder would be, as if they were ears; and the patient cannot bring his hand to its place, nor move in any way; and similarly, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you can clearly discern it by touching; and this type of dislocation is not simply about returning when it is recent, or where the child feels ill.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is for the minister to lift the hand of the sick person upwards, then place stools under their seat and gently elevate the joint back to its original position; then the minister lifts the hand and extends it upwards before setting them down again, and in a short time they will be healed.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	 And if it does not come as we have said in the past days, then the patient should be bathed in warm water; and treated gently with softening and soothing substances like an infusion of althaea and fenugreek and melilotus in water, and thus treated; then place the child on his back, and put a strap under the armpit equal neither too soft nor too hard, then position the heel of the foot onto the strap, and gently lift the shoulder blade, and massage the affected hand; and other treatments involve dyeing the top of the affected arm so that it does not move downwards; that shoulder returns immediately, and if you observe the child according to this method: and have an adult present who is taller than the child; and position themselves on the side opposite to the ailing shoulder, and place the shoulder underneath the armpit of the affected arm, and lift the shoulder upwards so that the child hangs downward, and other treatments involve massaging the affected hand towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	 And if the patient is too lightweight, strengthen them with something heavy, so that the dislocation now returns.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	 And the joint can also be treated in another way: and it is that one makes a long stick of iron and places it into the ground so that the shoulder is level with the nipple, neither too large nor too narrow; then put it under the patient but ensure there are sheets on top, and the limb should be as long as the shaft; then extend their hand to another side formally, and the joint will return quickly to its place; and if it does not return for all these reasons that we have mentioned, make this treatment: take a stick of iron two arms wide and four fingers thick, which has a head recessed so that muscles can enter on either side from below the armpit, in accordance with this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then wrap the head with soft cloth so that it does not touch the patient, then place under the saddle of the shoulder. Extend your arms above the length and tie the shoulder to the length, placing the arm at the top hand, then put one arm over a wide shelf bar, with hands hanging downwards, leaving the body suspended on the other side: the joint will be held in place now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is done in any way possible, then place under the saddle an equal thread of wool and put the poultice prepared with powdered molasses, along with incense and frankincense all over the shoulder and around, then stretch below the saddle promptly, twist the bandage on top of the poultice, and wrap it around his neck, with hands hanging thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	It is necessary that he moves little, as long as the limb is comforted, for it will heal sooner; and then move more after 5 or 6 days, and move it; and if it is firm and not softened, then it is well-healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	 If the joint is forcefully out of place due to moisture or another reason, it must be managed with three fire-cauterizations as previously described in this chapter or book on cauldration.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and it dislocates again after 6 days, and the joint does not hold, nor can lift any arm upward, then understand that either the nerve at the head of the shoulder is cut or extended or softened; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Dislocations towards the thigh and limbs or behind are made by impact, with hand extension, and another lever is applied; care for it until it becomes healthy again.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing comes weakness in the limb and tremors of movement, so often does the patient suffer painfully until the tremors are alleviated, and it returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	From the displacement of the shoulder blade
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the elbow is dislocated by bends and rebounds; if it has been dislocated from all sides, especially in front and behind, then the dislocation cannot be reduced, as it can be clearly seen and felt; and it dislocates according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	 And when you join the injured limb with its proper position, if it is clearly visible to be seen.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	 For the joint is lifted and cannot bend the arm or reach its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary that you reset them as soon as abscesses come to the surface, for if abscesses emerge, the repositioning would be grievous; and sometimes they cannot be reset at all, especially when they are in the back; this kind of dislocation is worse than others, and causes greater pain, and may even result in death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	When restoration is as such that it can be brought back, extend its hand to your two hands; and spread its arms wide, and the fingers following the course around, above and below, place the joint with its fingers together or at the root of its palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, when it comes back while doubling its hand to its own hand and at the root of the palm that has been dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	 And if it does not return to its place, apply strong extension; and two assistants extend the arm, and tie off one side with bandages, so that it cannot move during extension; then turn the arm from each side, after wrapping a double-width long cloth around it; when you have brought the joint close to their hand, anoint of any oil to soften the joint, then place the joint firmly until it returns; and once it is in its place, apply a dry embalmment with egg white, strain firmly, and stretch the arm toward the injured side, leaving it bound for several days, then release.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, release the sling, and leave it; and if you see that the joint does not tighten well, restart with dusting and binding, leaving it for several days until it is securely fixed; then release it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	 And if it feels tightness after the joint's resetting and it moves, then bathe and rub well, applying pressure until relieved; or place greased sheep fat on the joint, leave for one day and night, then bandage, and have them take a bath; when they sweat, quickly rub the joint again, replace the fat, and take another bath; thus do this two or three times until healed; if you see it, apply moistened wheat flour warmed with butter to strain upon.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The dislocation of the hand occurs, and its repositioning is easy compared to other joints; it must be promptly returned to its place within the same hour as it becomes dislocated, lest it swell or an abscess develop quickly.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	 The resets are such that you place the affected hand under a table, stretching the fingers out and align them evenly so that they can fit their palm against the joint's appearance, holding it until everything is back in order; then you should check if it has been properly realigned; thereafter, have the patient place their back of the hand under a table at full extension for resets.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	 And if the dislocation is in the back of the hand, put the patient's hand on a table, and the healer places his hand over that appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	 If it returns now, this is well; if not, strain the head of an aspenshaw with calming balm and leave as such until reassessment occurs.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	 And if it cannot endure any longer and you are unable to reset it after several days, the joint remains dislocated; and neither this nor that is possible for the patient when their hands become weak, and they can no longer grip anything: then declare that a nerve or artery has been cut, or there is no other remedy but to reset with fire near the wound, which may not yield any further results.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hands are at rest, place them on the splint as we have said, then strain and leave it for 5 days, then release and let be so.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it cannot move well, and there is any weakness, so rub with warm water, and massage until it feels smooth.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	From dislocations of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	 Never are the two of the hand dislocated to either side, nor to the back of the palm or belly; then they rejoin, and dislocation is put into place in your pockets as long as it returns, then support the head of the joint, and move towards the part where it was disjoined; leave it for two days, then on that day make it even, and again secure it, as we have said, and the next day dislocate it, and make it move, and rejoin the ligament; do this often until it is tightened, and do likewise if it is dislocated at the belly of the hand, and do as you did before, until it is sound; similarly, do so when dislocated from another part.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	The relaxation of the spinal column of the back.
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the spine of the back or neck is dislocated, and there are several dislocations, there is no remedy, as it quickly kills the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	 The excrements rise forcefully without voluntary action and cannot be held, resulting in softening of various members such as the legs or both arms or one; often the spine is dislocated into four parts; those that shift towards the back are called "gilbositez"; treatment for this involves resetting if gilbositez originated from childhood: if there is no cure or healing throughout.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	 Those resulting from falls or blows or similar things are said by ancient methods of treatment with great words, where there is no significant benefit; but I have shortened it according to my intention and formed remedies in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	 I say that in the swelling that comes to the thigh front, there is no remedy or health; and similarly those that come straight into the sides, which cannot be treated except for those specifically coming onto the back, as I have said; and it must be that the patient lies stretched out on their face with a length equal, and be strained off from underneath them so they do not lie flat; then place two tiles of earth firmly at the head, and another under the feet, and tie a band around the hips of the ill person, and another around the legs, and knees, and ankles; and two ministers know the bands, one to the head and one to the feet, among the two tiles; and they are well fastened as we have said, and the priest places his hands on the spine firmly until it straightens.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	 If it does not return with this treatment, take a stick three arms' length long, and place the patient on their side, head on the edge of the table, then position the stick under the shoulder; insert the middle of the stick along the spine; then align the feet using the other end of the stick, pressing firmly until it returns to its place; if so, turn them in a cradle that turns towards the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	 And that you insert two ties at the top of the patient's arm on one side and towards the feet on the other, with an inch of space between each tie, both above and below; have one hole through each tie or turn it right, ensuring they are firmly secured so they do not move; between each pair of ties, insert a turning pin, as we've mentioned, with two small pins at the same length to turn the cradle. Then attach the line among the ropes on one side of the cradle toward the head and the other line towards the feet on the opposite cradle; each minister turns their cradle along its entire length, while the master aligns the spine as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	 When they are equalized, place an absorptive dressing with plenty of wool, then the poultices, and then a splint from a tablet three fingers thick to secure the joint's location and the healthy part of the spine, then bind it with a bandage as we have said, and apply subtle nourishment to the patient until he is well; and if anything comes in at the end of recovery, administer softening and soothing medicines, along with the splint that we have mentioned earlier; on no occasion should one insert a piece of lead, nor does such an appearance occur in the rear spine causing dislocations; it is the bone cracking, therefore there should be no presumption: perhaps it would bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	For hip dislocations
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Sections that assert hip and shoulder joints are only from dislocations, not like other joints; the hip joint is dislocated in four parts: inside and outside, front and back; more inner than others, less forward and backward.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	 And the knowledge of its dislocation within is such that when joining the injured leg with the healthy one, it appears longer and opens more on the injured joint than the sound, and the injured cannot double their knee at fire; and there are legs which are swollen due to a hot abscess, because the hip's head comes near.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of those who come in later, such accidents are opposite to these before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	When it occurs in one who is before you, the sign is that they straighten their leg as completed; however, do not double bend the knee causing pain, and if you want them to walk, they cannot do so, retaining urine, swelling of the limb increases, and when walking, passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	When it occurs in one who is behind you, the sign is that they cannot expand their knee or double bend it, and that leg is more crooked than the other, swelling is softened, and the head of the thigh reaches up to below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The return of this kind of dislocation is that one should not assume the dislocation was present initially and it persists according to its nature, there is no treatment; and it must not be assumed that it has healed.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	In those cases where the dislocation is fresh, and there are four ways of dislocating, quickly return the joint to its place, push it back in and out, and move it to the right and left; perhaps it will come back on its own without needing further treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	 And if it does not return in this manner, you must prepare the patient with strong medicine, and keep the leg elevated by two hands or tie at the knee; another method extends its hand over like putting his palms under its soles, then strains gently at the ligament near the hip; another touches the neck of the ligament; and they stretch all at once, until the injured is raised from the ground completely, and hangs suspended.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common in four similar cases, and if the dislocation has been reset, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	 If not, one must attend to its appearance when the dislocation is in the jaw, it is necessary that you elevate the patient's chin on their uninjured side, then place the ligature at the base of the thigh, and the part out from under the angle, then extend the ligature upward toward the angle; then engage other ministers with his arms, and embrace the large jaw of the injured thigh, and extend it fully forward: it will return to its place now; and this manner of dislocation is easier than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	 And if you cannot hold it in the manner we have described, you should bind both feet of the injured together with a strong band above the heels and on the knees, and let the injured leg be extended two fingers more than the other; then hang from the head of a beam, and from the ground two arms lengthwise; then command another minister to embrace the thigh's top, and have others hanging with the patient, who fully grasp the thigh, for the joint returns quickly now.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	 When the dislocation is at the end, restrain the patient as described in those with gilbosity, and properly straighten the affected limb and foot likewise; then apply ties at head and other joints, then insert a billet between the buttocks near the deformed area of the afflicted person; and wrap moistened bandages around it so that it does not move the patient, then extend each minister towards him, and have mirrors placed equally in his hand to align the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	 If it returns, this is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	 If not, place on a table and press as described in cases of gilbosity, and restrain the patient by their strong side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it must be stretched with the sick leg quickly, and as I have said; place their pain over the sick side, then press with the other hand, and extend down towards the groin.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 If the dislocation is below, it is not appropriate to stretch the patient upwards or lift them off the ground, but rather they should lie as if their hip had been dislocated previously while lying on two pillows; then place something under their face, extend the limb as mentioned earlier, and apply pressure above the joint table; when the patient extends their legs, they will be equal. Then prop up the buttocks, put the plaster, and strain with a bandage so that the hip does not move. They should rest for three or four days, then release it, place something underne... If you see them as equal, strain again as before, and leave it for three days; then they can walk gently until the limb is strengthened.
de la dislocation dou genoil	Of shoulder dislocation
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The joint can be dislocated in three ways: into the bone and out of it, behind, and not forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 When the signs are such that you command the patient to bend his leg at the hip, and if it does not reach the hip, know that it is dislocated; and its restoration so is that you make the patient sit upright, extend his leg as much as he can, place your back against his face, and place your foot under yours; then take his knee in your palms, draw between your thumbs, then bend both shins properly; another method extends his foot until the joint returns to its place, and the sign is that it gently aligns with the hip; apply a plaster over it, raise the leg towards the hip, bandage them together firmly for 3 or 4 days, then untie; and do not allow the patient to move as long as the limb is supported.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	 And if the limb is not fixed, then it must be firmly extended as we have said in treating the knee, until it is straightened.
de la dislocation dou talon	on the ankle's dislocation
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heel is sometimes moved but never completely set right or wrong; within and without.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	 And the signs are such that the ankle is swollen, and one should gently try before reaching the part where it has dislocated: gentle attempts of repositioning must be done with hands when touched lightly only.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	 And when it is completely dislocated, one must have the patient lie down straight, with helpers supporting his leg upwards at the ankle; then grip the foot with your right hand, and move it towards you twice, then elevate it higher; then place the foot firmly above. Repeat this process as we've described - lifting and pulling on the foot; if it returns, that's good; if not, start over again because it will return; and if it cannot be brought back this way, make the patient lie down with their back to the ground, and place a firm strap between their thighs so they do not twitch. Adjust the straps evenly around them to keep the body stable while stretching occurs; then put bands equally on both sides of the dislocation using your hands or a tie, positioned over the neck of the foot; next extend each band evenly, and let the strap remain between thighs to hold in place during extension. Then grip the joint back into place with one hand while another helper supports the healthy leg below, then the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	 When it reaches the proper point, apply the dressing and plug into place, tighten firmly, bind the lump to the leg, and protect any veins behind the ankle so that the ties are not too tight; then let it rest for 2 or  three days, and if the ties relax, retighten the bandage; then release on the fourth day or a quarter of one, and advise the patient to walk with crutches for four days; and if they progress before this period, there is no assurance that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess appears there, it is necessary to soothe it as we have said elsewhere, until it becomes healthy again.
des dois	From the dislocation of both arms and legs
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When both arms or legs are dislocated, they must be stretched out with care, and it is a light task.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the dislocation is in any part of your lower back or foot, it must be that you make the patient sit upright on a flat surface or table directly underneath them, and place their leg under the affected joints, then press firmly onto the leg; and when they are even again, and nothing appears amiss, put two fingers' width of cotton padding beneath the sole of their foot, then bandage tightly, and let it rest for three days before releasing.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	Of wounds and of dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	 When a wound occurs with dislocation and you see it must be restored, often the patient dies: so do not presume in its treatment unless you are skilled in the art and have practiced it extenscriously, and if you are compassionate and merciful and slow to act; and at first use things that calm abscesses quickly, and leave the sick person in God's hands, unless you see hope of health; and when you see hope, then reset the limb into place as soon as possible so that inflammation may subside; and once the limb is set properly, apply matters that soothe an inflamed abscess and treat the wound accordingly with dried ointments; and if there is dislocation with bone fracture and small bones are exposed or visible, do as we have said in simple illnesses; but guard against falling into fear, according to what I have said, because it brings consequences according to your Creator, and for the wisdom of using your weapons and body.
Amen	 Amen
